   <h1 id="firstHeading" class="firstHeading" lang="en">Federal subjects of Russia</h1> 
   <div id="bodyContent" class="mw-body-content"> 
    <div id="siteSub" class="noprint">
     From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia
    </div> 
    <div id="contentSub"></div> 
    <div id="contentSub2"></div> 
    <div id="jump-to-nav"></div> <a class="mw-jump-link" href="#mw-head">Jump to navigation</a> <a class="mw-jump-link" href="#searchInput">Jump to search</a>

     <div class="mw-parser-output">
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       This article is about the federal constituent units. For the grouping of regions by a Presidential Decree, see <a href="/wiki/Federal_districts_of_Russia" title="Federal districts of Russia">Federal districts of Russia</a>.
      </div> 
      <p class="mw-empty-elt"> </p> 
      <div class="shortdescription nomobile noexcerpt noprint searchaux" style="display:none">
       Official constitutional top-level political division of Russia
      </div>

         <td style="padding:0.3em 0.4em 0.3em;font-weight:bold;border-top: 1px solid #aaa; border-bottom: 1px solid #aaa;"> <a href="/wiki/File:Flag_of_Russia.svg" class="image"><img alt="Flag of Russia.svg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/f3/Flag_of_Russia.svg/32px-Flag_of_Russia.svg.png" decoding="async" width="32" height="21" class="noviewer" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/f3/Flag_of_Russia.svg/48px-Flag_of_Russia.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/f3/Flag_of_Russia.svg/64px-Flag_of_Russia.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="900" data-file-height="600"></a>&nbsp;<a href="/wiki/Portal:Russia" title="Portal:Russia">Russia portal</a> 
          <div class="hlist" style="text-align:center;font-weight:normal;">

        <tr>
         <td style="text-align:right;font-size:115%;padding-top: 0.6em;"><style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r992953826">.mw-parser-output .navbar{display:inline;font-size:88%;font-weight:normal}.mw-parser-output .navbar-collapse{float:left;text-align:left}.mw-parser-output .navbar-boxtext{word-spacing:0}.mw-parser-output .navbar ul{display:inline-block;white-space:nowrap;line-height:inherit}.mw-parser-output .navbar-brackets::before{margin-right:-0.125em;content:"[ "}.mw-parser-output .navbar-brackets::after{margin-left:-0.125em;content:" ]"}.mw-parser-output .navbar li{word-spacing:-0.125em}.mw-parser-output .navbar-mini abbr{font-variant:small-caps;border-bottom:none;text-decoration:none;cursor:inherit}.mw-parser-output .navbar-ct-full{font-size:114%;margin:0 7em}.mw-parser-output .navbar-ct-mini{font-size:114%;margin:0 4em}.mw-parser-output .infobox .navbar{font-size:100%}.mw-parser-output .navbox .navbar{display:block;font-size:100%}.mw-parser-output .navbox-title .navbar{float:left;text-align:left;margin-right:0.5em}</style>
          <div class="navbar plainlinks hlist navbar-mini">
           <ul>
            <li class="nv-view"><a href="/wiki/Template:Politics_of_Russia" title="Template:Politics of Russia"><abbr title="View this template">v</abbr></a></li>
            <li class="nv-talk"><a href="/wiki/Template_talk:Politics_of_Russia" title="Template talk:Politics of Russia"><abbr title="Discuss this template">t</abbr></a></li>
            <li class="nv-edit"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template:Politics_of_Russia&amp;action=edit"><abbr title="Edit this template">e</abbr></a></li>
           </ul>
          </div></td>
        </tr>
       </tbody>
      </table> 
      <p>The <b>federal subjects of Russia</b>, also referred to as the <b>subjects of the Russian Federation</b> (<a href="/wiki/Russian_language" title="Russian language">Russian</a>: <span lang="ru">субъекты Российской Федерации</span>, <i>subyekty Rossiyskoy Federatsii</i>) or simply as the <b>subjects of the federation</b> (<a href="/wiki/Russian_language" title="Russian language">Russian</a>: <span lang="ru">субъекты федерации</span> <i>subyekty federatsii</i>), are the <a href="/wiki/Constituent_entity" class="mw-redirect" title="Constituent entity">constituent entities</a> of <a href="/wiki/Russia" title="Russia">Russia</a>, its top-level political divisions according to the <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Russia" title="Constitution of Russia">Constitution of Russia</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1">[1]</a></sup> Since March&nbsp;18, 2014, the Russian Federation constitutionally consists of 85 federal subjects.<sup id="cite_ref-Constitution65_2-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Constitution65-2">[2]</a></sup> The two located on the <a href="/wiki/Crimea" title="Crimea">Crimean Peninsula</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sevastopol" title="Sevastopol">Sevastopol</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Crimea" title="Republic of Crimea">Republic of Crimea</a>, <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_General_Assembly_Resolution_68/262" title="United Nations General Assembly Resolution 68/262"> are not internationally recognized</a> as part of Russia. </p>
      <p>According to the Russian Constitution, the Russian Federation consists of <a href="/wiki/Republics_of_Russia" title="Republics of Russia">republics</a>, <a href="/wiki/Krais_of_Russia" title="Krais of Russia">krais</a>, <a href="/wiki/Oblasts_of_Russia" title="Oblasts of Russia">oblasts</a>, <a href="/wiki/Federal_cities_of_Russia" title="Federal cities of Russia">cities of federal importance</a>, an <a href="/wiki/Autonomous_Oblasts_of_Russia" class="mw-redirect" title="Autonomous Oblasts of Russia">autonomous oblast</a> and <a href="/wiki/Autonomous_okrugs_of_Russia" title="Autonomous okrugs of Russia">autonomous okrugs</a>, all of which are equal subjects of the Russian Federation.<sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">[3]</a></sup> Three <a href="/wiki/Federal_cities_of_Russia" title="Federal cities of Russia">Russian cities of federal importance</a> (Moscow, Saint Petersburg, and Sevastopol) have a status of both city and separate federal subject which comprises other cities and towns (<a href="/wiki/Zelenograd" title="Zelenograd">Zelenograd</a>, <a href="/wiki/Troitsk,_Moscow" title="Troitsk, Moscow">Troitsk</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kronstadt" title="Kronstadt">Kronstadt</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kolpino,_Saint_Petersburg" title="Kolpino, Saint Petersburg">Kolpino</a>, etc.) within each federal city—keeping older structures of postal addresses. In 1993 the Russian Federation comprised 89&nbsp;federal subjects. By 2008, the number of federal subjects had decreased to&nbsp;83 because of several <a href="#Mergers">mergers</a>. In 2014 Sevastopol and the Republic of Crimea became the 84th and 85th federal subjects of Russia.<sup id="cite_ref-Treaty_4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Treaty-4">[4]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Reuters_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Reuters-5">[5]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Every federal subject has its own <a href="/wiki/Governor_(Russia)" title="Governor (Russia)">head</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Regional_parliaments_of_Russia" title="Regional parliaments of Russia">parliament</a>, and a constitutional court. Each federal subject has its own constitution and legislation. Subjects have equal rights in relations with federal government bodies.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup> The federal subjects have equal representation—two delegates each—in the <a href="/wiki/Federation_Council_of_Russia" class="mw-redirect" title="Federation Council of Russia">Federation Council</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Upper_house" title="Upper house">upper house</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Federal_Assembly_of_Russia" class="mw-redirect" title="Federal Assembly of Russia">Federal Assembly</a>. They do, however, differ in the degree of <a href="/wiki/Autonomous_area" class="mw-redirect" title="Autonomous area">autonomy</a> they enjoy (<a href="/wiki/Asymmetric_federalism" title="Asymmetric federalism">asymmetric federalism</a>). </p>
      <p>Post-Soviet Russia formed during the history of the <a href="/wiki/Russian_Soviet_Federative_Socialist_Republic" title="Russian Soviet Federative Socialist Republic">Russian Soviet Federative Socialist Republic</a> within the <a href="/wiki/USSR" class="mw-redirect" title="USSR">USSR</a> and did not change at the time of the <a href="/wiki/Dissolution_of_the_Soviet_Union" title="Dissolution of the Soviet Union">dissolution of the Soviet Union</a> in 1991. In 1992, during so-called "<a href="/wiki/Parade_of_sovereignties" title="Parade of sovereignties">parade of sovereignties</a>", <a href="/wiki/Nationalisms_in_Russia" title="Nationalisms in Russia">separatist sentiments</a> and the <a href="/wiki/War_of_Laws" title="War of Laws">War of Laws</a> within Russia, the Russian regions signed the <a href="/wiki/Federation_Treaty" class="mw-redirect" title="Federation Treaty">Federation Treaty</a> (<a href="/wiki/Russian_language" title="Russian language">Russian</a>: <span lang="ru">Федеративный договор</span> <i>Federativny Dogovor</i>),<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup> establishing and regulating the current inner composition of Russia, based on the division of authorities and powers among Russian government bodies and government bodies of constituent entities. The Federation Treaty was included in the text of the <a href="/wiki/Russian_Constitution_of_1978" title="Russian Constitution of 1978">1978 Constitution of the Russian SFSR</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> The current <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Russia" title="Constitution of Russia">Constitution of Russia</a>, adopted by national referendum on 12 December 1993, came into force on <span class="mw-formatted-date" title="1993-12-25">December 25, 1993</span> and abolished the model of the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_republic_(system_of_government)" title="Soviet republic (system of government)">Soviet system of government</a> introduced in 1918 by <a href="/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin" title="Vladimir Lenin">Vladimir Lenin</a> and based on the right to secede from the country and on unlimited sovereignty of federal subjects (in practice secession was never allowed), which conflicts with the country's integrity and federal laws. The new constitution eliminated a number of legal conflicts, reserved the rights of the regions, introduced local self-government and did not grant the Soviet-era right to secede from the country. In the late 1990s and early 2000s, the political system became <i>de jure</i> closer to other modern <a href="/wiki/Federal_republic" title="Federal republic">federal states with a republican form of government</a> in the world.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> In the 2000s, following the policy of <a href="/wiki/Vladimir_Putin" title="Vladimir Putin">Vladimir Putin</a> and of the <a href="/wiki/United_Russia" title="United Russia">United Russia</a> party (<a href="/wiki/Dominant-party_system" title="Dominant-party system">dominant party</a> in all federal subjects), the Russian parliament changed the distribution of tax revenues, reduced the number of elections in the regions and gave more power to the federal authorities. </p>

      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Terminology">Terminology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Federal_subjects_of_Russia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Terminology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <p>An official government translation of the <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Russia" title="Constitution of Russia">Constitution of Russia</a> in Article&nbsp;5 states: "1. The Russian Federation shall consist of <a href="/wiki/Republics_of_Russia" title="Republics of Russia">republics</a>, <a href="/wiki/Krais_of_Russia" title="Krais of Russia">krais</a>, <a href="/wiki/Oblasts_of_Russia" title="Oblasts of Russia">oblasts</a>, <a href="/wiki/Federal_cities_of_Russia" title="Federal cities of Russia">cities of federal significance</a>, an <a href="/wiki/Autonomous_oblasts_of_Russia" class="mw-redirect" title="Autonomous oblasts of Russia">autonomous oblast</a> and <a href="/wiki/Autonomous_okrugs_of_Russia" title="Autonomous okrugs of Russia">autonomous okrugs</a>, which shall have equal rights as constituent entities of the Russian Federation."<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Another translation of the <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Russia" title="Constitution of Russia">Constitution of Russia</a> gives for article 65: "<i>The Russian Federation includes the following subjects of the Russian Federation:</i>".<sup id="cite_ref-constitution.ru_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-constitution.ru-10">[10]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>How to translate the Russian term was discussed during the 49th annual <a href="/wiki/American_Translators_Association" title="American Translators Association">American Translators Association</a> conference in <a href="/wiki/Orlando" class="mw-redirect" title="Orlando">Orlando</a>, in which Tom Fennel, a freelance translator, argued that the term "constituent entity of the Russian Federation" should be preferred to "subject".<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup> This recommendation is also shared by Tamara Nekrasova, Head of Translation Department, Goltsblat <a href="/wiki/Berwin_Leighton_Paisner" title="Berwin Leighton Paisner">BLP</a>, who in her "Traps &amp; Mishaps in Legal Translation" presentation in Paris stated that "<i>constituent entity of the Russian Federation</i> is more appropriate than <i>subject of the Russian Federation</i> (subject would be OK for a monarchy)".<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup> </p> 
      <table class="wikitable sortable"> 
       <tbody>
        <tr>

         <th rowspan="2" width="150"><a href="/wiki/ISO_3166-2:RU" title="ISO 3166-2:RU">ISO 3166-2:RU</a> (ISO 3166-2 Newsletter II-2 (2010-06-30)) </th>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <th>(Cyrillic) </th> 
         <th>(Latin) </th> 
         <th>Official<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup> </th>

         <td data-sort-value="" style="background: #ececec; color: #2C2C2C; vertical-align: middle; text-align: center;" class="table-na">N/A </td>

      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Types">Types</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Federal_subjects_of_Russia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Types">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div class="center">
       <div class="floatnone">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Map_of_federal_subjects_of_Russia_(2014).svg" class="image" title="Federal subjects of Russia."><img alt="Federal subjects of Russia." src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/Map_of_federal_subjects_of_Russia_%282014%29.svg/690px-Map_of_federal_subjects_of_Russia_%282014%29.svg.png" decoding="async" width="690" height="380" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/Map_of_federal_subjects_of_Russia_%282014%29.svg/1035px-Map_of_federal_subjects_of_Russia_%282014%29.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/Map_of_federal_subjects_of_Russia_%282014%29.svg/1380px-Map_of_federal_subjects_of_Russia_%282014%29.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="282"></a>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Each federal subject belongs to one of the following types: </p> 
      <table class="wikitable sortable"> 
       <tbody>
        <tr> 
         <th>Legend </th> 
         <th>Description </th>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r981673959">.mw-parser-output .legend{page-break-inside:avoid;break-inside:avoid-column}.mw-parser-output .legend-color{display:inline-block;min-width:1.25em;height:1.25em;line-height:1.25;margin:1px 0;text-align:center;border:1px solid black;background-color:transparent;color:black}.mw-parser-output .legend-text{}</style>
          <div class="legend">
           <span class="legend-color" style="background-color:#FFEC77; color:black; -webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;">&nbsp;</span>&nbsp;46&nbsp;<a href="/wiki/Oblasts_of_Russia" title="Oblasts of Russia">oblasts</a>
          </div> </td> 
         <td>The most common type of federal subject with a governor and locally elected legislature. Commonly named after their administrative centres. </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td>
          <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959">
          <div class="legend">
           <span class="legend-color" style="background-color:#00C160; color:black; -webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;">&nbsp;</span>&nbsp;22&nbsp;<a href="/wiki/Republics_of_Russia" title="Republics of Russia">republics</a>
          </div> </td> 
         <td>Nominally autonomous,<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Saunders_2019_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Saunders_2019-15">[15]</a></sup> each with its own constitution, language, and legislature but represented by the federal government in international affairs. Each is home to a specific <a href="/wiki/Ethnic_groups_in_Russia" title="Ethnic groups in Russia">ethnic minority</a>. </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td>
          <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959">
          <div class="legend">
           <span class="legend-color" style="background-color:#FF9400; color:black; -webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;">&nbsp;</span>&nbsp;9&nbsp;<a href="/wiki/Krais_of_Russia" title="Krais of Russia">krais</a>
          </div> </td> 
         <td>Essentially the same as oblasts. The title "krai" ("frontier" or "territory") is historic, related to geographic (frontier) position in a certain period of history. The current krais are not related to frontiers. </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td>
          <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959">
          <div class="legend">
           <span class="legend-color" style="background-color:#006989; color:white; -webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;">&nbsp;</span>&nbsp;4&nbsp;<a href="/wiki/Autonomous_okrugs_of_Russia" title="Autonomous okrugs of Russia">autonomous okrugs</a>
          </div> </td> 
         <td>Occasionally referred to as "autonomous district", "autonomous area", and "autonomous region", each with a substantial or predominant ethnic minority. </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td>
          <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959">
          <div class="legend">
           <span class="legend-color" style="background-color:#FF0037; color:black; -webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;">&nbsp;</span>&nbsp;3&nbsp;<a href="/wiki/Federal_cities_of_Russia" title="Federal cities of Russia">federal cities</a>
          </div> </td> 
         <td>Major cities that function as separate regions. </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td>
          <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959">
          <div class="legend">
           <span class="legend-color" style="background-color:#C300FF; color:black; -webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;">&nbsp;</span>&nbsp;1&nbsp;autonomous oblast
          </div> </td> 
         <td>The only autonomous oblast is the <a href="/wiki/Jewish_Autonomous_Oblast" title="Jewish Autonomous Oblast">Jewish Autonomous Oblast</a>. </td>
        </tr>
       </tbody>
      </table>

         <td>— </td> 
         <td style="text-align:center;"><a href="/wiki/File:Flag_of_Sevastopol.svg" class="image"><img alt="Flag of Sevastopol.svg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/Flag_of_Sevastopol.svg/45px-Flag_of_Sevastopol.svg.png" decoding="async" width="45" height="30" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/Flag_of_Sevastopol.svg/68px-Flag_of_Sevastopol.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/Flag_of_Sevastopol.svg/90px-Flag_of_Sevastopol.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="600" data-file-height="400"></a> </td> 
         <td style="text-align:center;"><a href="/wiki/File:COA_of_Sevastopol.svg" class="image"><img alt="COA of Sevastopol.svg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/COA_of_Sevastopol.svg/37px-COA_of_Sevastopol.svg.png" decoding="async" width="37" height="45" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/COA_of_Sevastopol.svg/56px-COA_of_Sevastopol.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/COA_of_Sevastopol.svg/74px-COA_of_Sevastopol.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="372" data-file-height="450"></a> </td> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/Federal_cities_of_Russia" title="Federal cities of Russia">federal city</a> </td>

      <style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r994654864">.mw-parser-output .refbegin{font-size:90%;margin-bottom:0.5em}.mw-parser-output .refbegin-hanging-indents>ul{list-style-type:none;margin-left:0}.mw-parser-output .refbegin-hanging-indents>ul>li,.mw-parser-output .refbegin-hanging-indents>dl>dd{margin-left:0;padding-left:3.2em;text-indent:-3.2em;list-style:none}.mw-parser-output .refbegin-100{font-size:100%}.mw-parser-output .refbegin-columns{margin-top:0.3em}.mw-parser-output .refbegin-columns dl,.mw-parser-output .refbegin-columns ol,.mw-parser-output .refbegin-columns ul{margin-top:0}.mw-parser-output .refbegin-columns li,.mw-parser-output .refbegin-columns dd{page-break-inside:avoid;break-inside:avoid-column}</style>
      <div class="refbegin" style=""> 
       <p><b>a.</b> <span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_anone"><a href="#ref_anone"><b><sup>^</sup></b></a></span> The largest city is also listed when it is different from the capital/administrative center. </p>
       <p><b>b.</b> <span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_bnone"><a href="#ref_bnone"><b><sup>^</sup></b></a></span> According to Article&nbsp;13 of the Charter of Leningrad Oblast, the governing bodies of the oblast are located in the city of <a href="/wiki/Saint_Petersburg" title="Saint Petersburg">St.&nbsp;Petersburg</a>. However, St.&nbsp;Petersburg is not officially named to be the administrative center of the oblast. </p>
       <p><b>c.</b> <span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_cnone"><a href="#ref_cnone"><b><sup>^</sup></b></a></span> According to Article&nbsp;24 of the Charter of Moscow Oblast, the governing bodies of the oblast are located in the city of <a href="/wiki/Moscow" title="Moscow">Moscow</a> and throughout the territory of Moscow Oblast. However, Moscow is not officially named to be the administrative center of the oblast. </p>
       <p><b>d.</b> <span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_dnone"><a href="#ref_dnone"><b><sup>^</sup></b></a></span> <a href="/wiki/Political_status_of_Crimea" title="Political status of Crimea">Not recognized internationally</a> as a part of Russia. </p>
       <p><b>e.</b> <span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_enone"><a href="#ref_enone"><b><sup>^</sup></b></a></span> In February 2000, the former code of 20 for the Chechen Republic was cancelled and replaced with code 95. License plate production was suspended due to the Chechen Wars, causing numerous issues, which in turn forced the region to use a new code. </p> 
      </div>

      <h2><span id="Mergers.2C_splits_and_internal_territorial_changes"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Mergers,_splits_and_internal_territorial_changes">Mergers, splits and internal territorial changes <span class="anchor" id="Mergers"></span></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Federal_subjects_of_Russia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Mergers, splits and internal territorial changes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div class="center">
       <div class="thumb tnone">
        <div class="thumbinner" style="width:752px;">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Russian_Subjects_merged.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/Russian_Subjects_merged.png/750px-Russian_Subjects_merged.png" decoding="async" width="750" height="601" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/Russian_Subjects_merged.png/1125px-Russian_Subjects_merged.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/2/29/Russian_Subjects_merged.png 2x" data-file-width="1130" data-file-height="905"></a> 
         <div class="thumbcaption">
          <div class="magnify">
           <a href="/wiki/File:Russian_Subjects_merged.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
          </div>Map of the federal subjects of Russia highlighting those that merged in the first decade of the 21st century (in yellow), and those whose merger has been discussed in the same decade (in orange)
         </div>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Starting in 2005, some of the federal subjects were merged into larger territories. In this process, six very sparsely populated subjects (comprising in total 0.3% of the population of Russia) were integrated into more populated subjects, with the hope that the economic development of those territories would benefit from the much larger means of their neighbours. The <a href="https://ru.wikipedia.org/wiki/%D0%9E%D0%B1%D1%8A%D0%B5%D0%B4%D0%B8%D0%BD%D0%B5%D0%BD%D0%B8%D0%B5_%D1%80%D0%B5%D0%B3%D0%B8%D0%BE%D0%BD%D0%BE%D0%B2_%D0%A0%D0%BE%D1%81%D1%81%D0%B8%D0%B8" class="extiw" title="ru:Объединение регионов России">merging process</a> was finished on 1 March 2008. No new mergers have been planned since March 2008. The six territories became "administrative-territorial regions with special status". They have large proportions of minorities, with Russians being a majority only in three of them. Four of those territories have a second official language in addition to Russian: <a href="/wiki/Buryat_language" title="Buryat language">Buryat</a> (in two of the merged territories), <a href="/wiki/Komi-Perm_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Komi-Perm language">Komi-Permian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Koryak_language" title="Koryak language">Koryak</a>. This is an exception: all the other official languages of Russia (other than Russian) are set by the Constitutions of its constituent Republics (<a href="/wiki/Mordovia" title="Mordovia">Mordovia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chechnya" title="Chechnya">Chechnya</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dagestan" title="Dagestan">Dagestan</a> etc.). The status of the "administrative-territorial regions with special status" has been a subject of criticism because it does not appear in the Constitution of the Russian Federation. </p> 
      <table class="wikitable sortable">

        </tr>

         <td>2007-03-11 </td> 
         <td>2008-03-01 </td> 
         <td style="text-align:center;">5, 5a </td> 
         <td style="text-align:center;">75 (5), 80 (5a) </td> 
         <td style="text-align:center;">92 </td> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/Chita_Oblast" title="Chita Oblast">Chita Oblast</a> (5) + <a href="/wiki/Agin-Buryat_Autonomous_Okrug" title="Agin-Buryat Autonomous Okrug">Agin-Buryat Autonomous Okrug</a> (5a) </td>

        </tr>
       </tbody>
      </table> 
      <p>In addition to those six territories that entirely ceased to be subjects of the Russian Federation and were downgraded to territories with special status, another three subjects have a status of subject but are simultaneously part of a more populated subject: </p> 
      <ul>
       <li><a href="/wiki/Nenets_Autonomous_Okrug" title="Nenets Autonomous Okrug">Nenets Autonomous Okrug</a> (2010 population of 42090) is a subject since 1993, but is also, according to its Constitution, a part of <a href="/wiki/Arkhangelsk_Oblast" title="Arkhangelsk Oblast">Arkhangelsk Oblast</a></li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Khanty-Mansi_Autonomous_Okrug" title="Khanty-Mansi Autonomous Okrug">Khanty-Mansi Autonomous Okrug</a> obtained autonomy in 1977, but is simultaneously part of <a href="/wiki/Tyumen_Oblast" title="Tyumen Oblast">Tyumen Oblast</a></li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Yamalo-Nenets_Autonomous_Okrug" title="Yamalo-Nenets Autonomous Okrug">Yamalo-Nenets Autonomous Okrug</a> obtained the status of subject in 1992 (after obtaining autonomy in 1977), but is also part of Tyumen Oblast.</li>
      </ul> 
      <p>With an estimated population of 49348 as of 2018, <a href="/wiki/Chukotka_Autonomous_Okrug" title="Chukotka Autonomous Okrug">Chukotka</a> is currently the least populated subject of Russia that is not part of a more populated subject. It was separated from <a href="/wiki/Magadan_Oblast" title="Magadan Oblast">Magadan Oblast</a> in 1993. Chukotka is one of the richest subjects of Russia (with a GRP per capita equivalent to that of Australia) and therefore does not fit in the pattern of merging a subject to benefit from the economic dynamism of the neighbour. </p>
      <p>In 1992, <a href="/wiki/Ingushetia" title="Ingushetia">Ingushetia</a> separated from <a href="/wiki/Chechnya" title="Chechnya">Chechnya</a>, both to stay away from the growing violence in Chechnya and as a bid to obtain the Eastern part of Northern Ossetia (it did not work: the Chechen conflict spread violence to Ingushetia, and North Ossetia retained its <a href="/wiki/Prigorodny_District,_North_Ossetia-Alania" class="mw-redirect" title="Prigorodny District, North Ossetia-Alania">Prigorodny District</a>). Those two Muslim republics, populated in vast majority (95%+) by closely related <a href="/wiki/Nakh_peoples" title="Nakh peoples">Vainakh people</a>, speaking <a href="/wiki/Vainakhish_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Vainakhish language">Vainakhish languages</a>, remain the two poorest subjects of Russia, with the GRP per capita of Ingushetia being equivalent to that of Iraq. According to 2016 statistics, however they are also the safest regions of Russia, and also have the lowest alcohol consumption, with alcohol poisoning at least 40 times lower than the national average.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Until 1994, <a href="/wiki/Sokolsky_District,_Nizhny_Novgorod_Oblast" title="Sokolsky District, Nizhny Novgorod Oblast">Sokolsky District, Nizhny Novgorod Oblast</a> was part of <a href="/wiki/Ivanovo_Oblast" title="Ivanovo Oblast">Ivanovo Oblast</a>. </p>
      <p>In 2011–2012, the territory of Moscow increased by 140% (to 2,511&nbsp;km<sup>2</sup> (970&nbsp;sq&nbsp;mi)) by acquiring part of <a href="/wiki/Moscow_Oblast" title="Moscow Oblast">Moscow Oblast</a>. </p>
      <p>On 13 May 2020, the governors of Arkhangelsk Oblast and Nenets Autonomous Okrug announced their plan to merge following the collapse of oil prices stemming from the <a href="/wiki/COVID-19_pandemic" title="COVID-19 pandemic">COVID-19 pandemic</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup> The process was scrapped on July 2.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup> </p>

      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sources">Sources</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Federal_subjects_of_Russia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Sources">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <ul>
       <li><span lang="ru" title="Russian language text">12 декабря 1993 г. «<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.consultant.ru/online/base/?req=doc;base=LAW;n=83686">Конституция Российской Федерации</a>», в ред. Федерального конституционного закона №7-ФКЗ от&nbsp;30 декабря 2008 г. Вступил в силу&nbsp;со дня официального опубликования. Опубликован: "Российская газета", №237, 25 декабря 1993 г.</span> (December 12, 1993 <i><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://translate.google.com/translate?hl=en&amp;sl=ru&amp;tl=en&amp;u=http://www.consultant.ru/online/base/?req=doc;base=LAW;n=83686">Constitution of the Russian Federation</a></i>, as amended by the Federal Constitutional Law&nbsp;#7-FKZ of&nbsp;December 30, 2008. Effective as of&nbsp;the official publication date.).</li>
      </ul>
